Alternate Unicode Encodings / Variation Selectors
Some glyphs may be used for more than one
unicode code point -- I don't recommend
doing this, better to use a reference --
but it is possible.
The latin "A", the greek "Alpha" and the
cyrillic "A" look very much the same.
On the other hand certain Mongolian and CJK
characters have multiple glyphs depending
on a unicode Variation Selector.
In the first case use a variation selector
of 0, in the second use the appropriate
codepoint.
Mark for Unlink, Remove Overlap before Generating
A few glyphs, like Aring, Ccedilla, Eogonek
are composed of two overlapping references.
Often it is desirable to retain the references
(so that changes made to the base glyph are
reflected in the composed glyph), but that
means you are stuck with overlapping contours.
This flag means that just before generating
the font, FontForge will unlink the references
and run remove overlap on them, while
 retaining the references in the SFD.
Don't display columns of 0s.
The OpenType lookup allows for up to 8 kinds
of data, but almost all kerning lookups will use just one.
Omitting the others makes the behavior clearer.
The height and depth fields are the metrics fields used
by TeX, they are corrected for optical distortion.
So 'x' and 'o' probably have the same height.
The Italic correction field is used by both TeX and the MS 'MATH'
table. It is used when joining slanted text (italic) to upright.
It is the amount of extra white space needed so the slanted text
will not run into the upright text.
A device table for italic correction.
Expects a comma separated list of <pixelsize>":"<adjustment>
As "9:-1,12:1,13:1"
In the MS 'MATH' table this value specifies where (horizontally)
an accent should be placed above the glyph. Vertical placement
is handled by other means
A device table for horizontal accent positioning.
Expects a comma separated list of <pixelsize>":"<adjustment>
As "9:-1,12:1,13:1"
Is this an extended shape (like a tall parenthesis)?
Extended shapes need special attention for vertical
superscript placement.
Brings up a dialog which gives fine control over
horizontal positioning of subscripts and superscripts
depending on their vertical positioning.
Ligature caret locations are used by a text editor
when it needs to draw a text edit caret inside a
ligature. This means there should be a caret between
each ligature component so if there are n components
there should be n-1 caret locations.
  You may adjust the caret locations themselves in the
outline glyph view (drag them from to origin to the
appropriate place).
A list of the names of pre defined glyphs which represent
bigger versions of the current glyph.
A really big version of this glyph may be made up of the
following component glyphs. They will be stacked either
horizontally or vertically. Glyphs marked as Extenders may
be removed or repeated (to make shorter or longer versions).
The StartLength is the length of the flat section at the
start of the glyph which may be overlapped with the previous
glyph, while the EndLength is the similar region at the end
of the glyph. The FullLength is the full length of the glyph.
The italic correction of the composed glyph. Should be independent of glyph size

some other glyph then it is useful to specify
the amount of whitespace surrounding the tile.

box of the contents, or specify the bounds
explicitly.

You must draw a line, with at most one additional point
  A linear gradient is represented by a line drawn
from its start point to its end point.
  A radial gradient is represented by a line drawn
from its center whose length is the ultimate radius.
If there is a single additional point, that point
represents the gradient's focus, if omitted the focus
is the same as the radius.
The gradient will be a linear gradient,
With the color change happening along
the line drawn in the view
The gradient will be a radial gradient,
With the color change happening in circles
starting at the focus (if specified) and
extending outward until it reaches the
specified radius.
Beyond the endpoints, the gradient takes on the color at the end-points
This does not work for PostScript linear gradients
Beyond the endpoints the gradient repeats itself
This does not work for PostScript gradients.
Beyond the endpoint the gradient repeats itself, but reflected.
This does not work for PostScript gradients

(between 0 and 255) which give the dash pattern
in em-units. So "10 10" will draw the first
10 units of a line, leave the next 10 blank,
draw the next 10, and so on.

The OFL is a community-approved software license designed for libre/open font projects. 
Fonts under the OFL can be used, studied, copied, modified, embedded, merged and redistributed while giving authors enough control and artistic integrity. For more details including an FAQ see http://scripts.sil.org/OFL. 
This font metadata will help users, designers and distribution channels to know who you are, how to contact you and what rights you are granting. 
When releasing modified versions, remember to add your additional notice, including any extra Reserved Font Name(s). 
Have fun designing open fonts!

The 'gasp' table gives you control over when grid-fitting and
anti-aliased rasterizing are done.
The table consists of an (ordered) list of pixel sizes each with
a set of flags. Those flags apply to all pixel sizes bigger than
the previous table entry but less than or equal to the current.
The list must be terminated with a pixel size of 65535.
Version 1 of the table contains two additional flags that
apply to MS's ClearType rasterizer.
The 'gasp' table only applies to truetype fonts.

collabclient_getState( fv ) %d %d
Please specify a new supplement for %.20s-%.20s
Known encoding could not be found
Enter either a wildcard pattern (to match glyph names)
 or a unicode encoding like "U+0065".
Unix style wildcarding is accepted:
Most characters match themselves
A "?" will match any single character
A "*" will match an arbitrary number of characters (including none)
An "[abd]" set of characters within square brackets will match any (single) character
A "{scmp,c2sc}" set of strings within curly brackets will match any string
So "a.*" would match "a." or "a.sc" or "a.swash"
While "a.{scmp,c2sc}" would match "a.scmp" or "a.c2sc"
And "a.[abd]" would match "a.a" or "a.b" or "a.d"

The font does not contain a glyph named %s.
The glyph named %s also occurs in the class on row %d which begins with %.20s...

Add entries to the lookup trying to make the optical
separation between all pairs of glyphs equal to this
value.
Any computed kerning change whose absolute value is less
that this will be ignored.
Normally kerning is based on achieving a constant (optical)
separation between glyphs, but occasionally it is desirable
to have a kerning table where the kerning is based on the
closest approach between two glyphs (So if the desired separ-
ation is 0 then the glyphs will actually be touching.
When doing autokerning, only move glyphs closer together,
so the kerning offset will be negative.
When adding a new class provide default kerning values
Between it and every class with which it interacts.

In this format you specify every kerning pair in which

In this format you define a series of glyph classes and
specify a matrix showing how each class interacts with all

FontForge will guess kerning classes for selected glyphs
FontForge will look at the glyphs selected in the font view
and will try to find groups of glyphs which are most alike
and generate kerning classes based on that information.
This is roughly (very roughly) the number off em-units
of error that two glyphs may have to belong in the same
class. This error is taken by comparing the two glyphs
to all other glyphs and summing the differences.
A small number here (like 2) means lots of small classes,
while a larger number (like 20) will mean fewer classes,
each with more glyphs.
When adding new entries provide default kerning values.

Apple and MS/Adobe differ about the format of truetype and opentype files.
This controls the default setting of the Apple checkbox in the
File->Generate Font dialog.
The main differences are:
 Bitmap data are stored in different tables
 Scaled composite glyphs are treated differently
 Use of GSUB rather than morx(t)/feat
 Use of GPOS rather than kern/opbd
 Use of GDEF rather than lcar/prop
If both this and OpenType are set, both formats are generated

engine, and to disambiguate this change has created a parallel set of script
tags (generally ending in '2') for Indic writing systems. If you are working
with the new system set this flag, if you are working with the old unset it.
(if you aren't doing Indic work, this flag is irrelevant).

When generating a font, ignore slight rounding errors for hints that should be at the top or bottom of the glyph. For example, you might like to set this to 0.02 so that 19.999 will be considered 20. But only for the hint width value.

FontForge will use this namelist when assigning
glyph names to code points in a new font.
Once upon a time, Adobe assigned PUA (public use area) encodings
for many stylistic variants of characters (small caps, old style
numerals, etc.). Adobe no longer believes this to be a good idea,
and recommends that these encodings be ignored.
 The assignments were originally made because most applications
could not handle OpenType features for accessing variants. Adobe
now believes that all apps that matter can now do so. Applications
like Word and OpenOffice still can't handle these features, so
 fontforge's default behavior is to ignore Adobe's current
recommendations.
Note: This does not affect figuring out unicode from the font's encoding,
it just controls determining unicode from a name.
Allow the full unicode character set in glyph names.
This does not conform to adobe's glyph name standard.
Such names should be for internal use only and
should NOT end up in production fonts.
When displaying a list of glyph names
(or sometimes just a single glyph name)
FontForge will add the unicode character
the name refers to in parenthesis after
the name. It does this because some names
are obscure.
Some people would prefer not to see this,
so this preference item lets you turn off
 this behavior
FontForge supports two different helper applications to do autotracing

use this option to tell FontForge which to pick.

Instructions in a TrueType font refer to
points by number, so if you edit a glyph
in such a way that some points have different
numbers (add points, remove them, etc.) then
the instructions will be applied to the wrong
points with disasterous results.
  Normally FontForge will remove the instructions
if it detects that the points have been renumbered
in order to avoid the above problem. You may turn
this behavior off -- but be careful!
When copying glyphs from the font view, also copy the
glyphs' truetype instructions.
Changing the width of a glyph
changes the widths of all accented
glyphs based on it.
Changing the left side bearing
of a glyph adjusts the lbearing
of other references in all accented
glyphs based on it.

The number of undo and redo operations to load from sfd files.
With this option you can disregard undo information while loading SFD files.

OpenTypeLoadHintEqualityTolerance
When importing an OpenType font, for the purposes of hinting spline points might not exactly match boundaries. For example, a point might be -0.0002 instead of exactly 0
This setting gives the user some control over this allowing a small tolerance value to be fed into the OpenType loading code.
Comparisons are then not performed for raw equality but for equality within tolerance (e.g., values within the range -0.0002 to 0.0002 will be considered equal to 0 when figuring out hints).

new fonts

(see NewFontsQuadratic).
When FontForge starts up, it loads the user interface theme from

If you wish to replace Adobe's OtherSubrs array (for Type1 fonts)
with an array of your own, set this to point to a file containing
a list of up to 14 PostScript subroutines. Each subroutine must
be preceded by a line starting with '%%%%' (any text before the
first '%%%%' line will be treated as an initial copyright notice).
The first three subroutines are for flex hints, the next for hint
substitution (this MUST be present), the 14th (or 13 as the
numbering actually starts with 0) is for counter hints.
The subroutines should not be enclosed in a [ ] pair.

one glyph in the fontview). If you have a clipboard manager
running it will force these to be exported with consequent
loss of data.

Check for _irrelevant control points
Control points are irrelevant if they are too close to the main
point to make a significant difference in the shape of the curve.
A control point is deemed irrelevant if the distance between it and the main
(end) point is less than this times the distance between the two end points
If two adjacent points on the same path are less than a few
emunits apart they will cause problems for some of FontForge's
commands. PostScript shouldn't care though.
Most font formats cannot specify adjacent points (or control points)
which are more than 32767 em-units apart in either the x or y direction
All paths should be closed loops, there should be no exposed endpoints

Check _outermost paths clockwise
FontForge internally uses paths drawn in a
clockwise direction. This lets you check that they are.
Before doing this test insure that
no paths self-intersect.
PostScript and TrueType require that when a path
reaches its maximum or minimum position
there must be a point at that location.
The PostScript Language Reference Manual (Appendix B) says that
an interpreter need not support paths with more than 1500 points.
I think this count includes control points. From PostScript's point
of view, all the contours in a character make up one path. Modern
interpreters tend to support paths with more points than this limit.
(Note a truetype font after conversion to PS will contain
twice as many control points)
PostScript and TrueType require that paths be drawn
in a clockwise direction. If you have a reference
that has been flipped then the paths in that reference will
probably be counter-clockwise. You should unlink it and do
Element->Correct direction on it.
Refs with bad tt transformation matrices
TrueType requires that all scaling and rotational
entries in a transformation matrix be between -2 and 2
TrueType glyphs can either contain references or contours.
Not both.
Refs with bad ps transformation matrices
Type1 and 2 fonts only support translation of references.
The first four entries of the transformation matrix should be
[1 0 0 1].
The Type 2 Charstring Reference (Appendix B) says that
subroutines may not be nested more than 10 deep. Each
nesting level for references requires one subroutine
level, and hints may require another level.
Refs with out of date point matching
If a glyph has been edited so that it has a different
number of points now, then any references
which use point matching and depended on that glyph's
point count will be incorrect.
Multiple refs with use-my-metrics
There may be at most one reference with the use-my-metrics bit set

hint exists without any points that lie on it.

it is because a stem is made up
of several segments, and one of them
has the wrong width.
Allows you to check that stems have consistent widths..
This checks if the character almost, but not exactly,
conforms to the requirements for a stem3 hint.
That is, either vertically or horizontally, there must
be exactly three hints, and they must have the same
width and they must be evenly spaced.

The Type 2 Charstring Reference (Appendix B) says that
there may be at most 96 horizontal and vertical stem hints
in a character.

or a glyph with hint masks should have no overlapping

The AFM file contains metrics information that many word-processors will read when using a PostScript
 font.
The AFM format allows some information about composites
(roughly the same as mark to base anchor classes) to be
included. However it tends to make AFM files huge as it
is not stored in an efficient manner.
The PFM file contains information Windows needs to install a PostScript
 font.
The tfm and enc files contain information TeX needs to install a PostScript
 font.
Do you want the font file to contain truetype hints? This will not
generate new instructions, it will just make use of whatever is associated
with each character.
Do you want the font file to contain the names of each glyph in the font?
Apple and MS/Adobe differ about the format of truetype and opentype files
This allows you to select which standard to follow for your font.
The main differences are:
 The requirements for the 'postscript' name in the name table conflict
 Bitmap data are stored in different tables
 Scaled composite characters are treated differently
 Use of GSUB rather than morx(t)/feat
 Use of GPOS rather than kern/opbd
 Use of GDEF rather than lcar/prop

generate an empty one with no signature info. A pointless table.

The FONTLOG allows you to keep a log of changes made to your font.
This option prepends a timestamp in the format YYMMDDHHMM to the filename and font-family name metadata.
FontForge can generate two styles of ttc file.
In the first each font is a separate entity
with no connection to other fonts. In the second
FontForge will attempt to use the same glyph table
for all fonts, merging duplicate glyphs. It will
also attempt to use the same space for tables in
different fonts which are bit by bit the same.
FontForge isn't always able to perform a merge, in
which case it falls back on generating independent
fonts within the ttc.
 FontForge cannot merge if:
  * The fonts have different em-sizes
  * Bitmaps are involved
  * The merged glyf table has more than 65534 glyphs
(Merging will take longer)
Put CFF fonts into the ttc rather than TTF.
 These seem to work on the mac and linux
 but are documented not to work on Windows.

Allow a match even if the search pattern has

Endpoints specify minimum length and direction only
If the search pattern is a single open contour
then do not match the end points. They merely
specify the direction from which the curve should
move toward the next point (which will be matched),
and the minimum distance between the first matched
point and the one before it. The endpoints of the
replace contour will also only be used for positioning.
This allows you to match a right angle corner
without needed to specify exactly how long the edges
are which form the right angle.
Only search characters selected in the fontview.
Normally we search all characters in the font.

Gaudeamus Ligature!
fontforge [options] [fontfiles]
	-last			 (loads the last sfd file closed)
	-recover none|auto|inquire|clean (control error recovery)
	-allglyphs		 (load all glyphs in the 'glyf' table
			 of a truetype collection)
	-nosplash		 (no splash screen)
	-quiet			 (don't print non-essential information to stderr)
	-unique			 (if a fontforge is already running open
			 all arguments in it and have this process exit)
	-display display-name	 (sets the X display)
	-depth val		 (sets the display depth if possible)
	-vc val			 (sets the visual class if possible)
	-cmap current|copy|private	 (sets the type of colormap)
	-dontopenxdevices	 (in case that fails)
	-sync			 (syncs the display, debugging)
	-keyboard ibm|mac|sun|ppc  (generates appropriate hotkeys in menus)
	-usecairo=yes|no  Use (or not) the cairo library for drawing
	-help			 (displays this message, and exits)
	-docs			 (displays this message, invokes a browser)
				 (Using the BROWSER environment variable)
	-version		 (prints the version of fontforge and exits)
	-library-status	 (prints information about optional libraries
				 and exits)
	-lang=py		 use python for scripts (may precede -script)
	-lang=ff		 use fontforge's legacy scripting language
	-script scriptfile	 (executes scriptfile)
		must be the first option (or follow -lang).
		All others passed to scriptfile.
	-dry scriptfile		 (syntax checks scriptfile)
		must be the first option. All others passed to scriptfile.
		Only for fontforge's own scripting language, not python.
	-c script-string	 (executes argument as scripting cmds)
		must be the first option. All others passed to the script.
FontForge will read postscript (pfa, pfb, ps, cid), opentype (otf),
	truetype (ttf,ttc), macintosh resource fonts (dfont,bin,hqx),
	and bdf and pcf fonts. It will also read its own format --
If no fontfiles are specified (and -new is not either and there's nothing
	to recover) then fontforge will produce an open font dlg.
If a scriptfile is specified then FontForge will not open the X display
	nor will it process any additional arguments. It will execute the
	scriptfile and give it any remaining arguments
If the first argument is an executable filename, and that file's first
	line contains "fontforge" then it will be treated as a scriptfile.
For more information see:
	http://fontforge.sourceforge.net/
Send bug reports to:	fontforge-devel@lists.sourceforge.net

 c=1 round

How many entries should there be in the cvt table?
TrueType does not support mixed references and contours.
If you want instructions for %.30s you should either:
 * Unlink the reference(s)
 * Copy the inline contours into their own (unencoded
    glyph) and make a reference to that.
TrueType Instructions for %.50s
TrueType does not support references which
are scaled by more than 200%%.  But %1$.30s
has been in %2$.30s. Any instructions
added would be meaningless.
The instructions for %.80s have changed. Do you want to lose those changes?

Your version of the freetype library does not contain the bytecode interpreter.

This glyph has no instructions. Adding instructions (a DELTA) may change its rasterization significantly.
When a curve passes very close to the center of a
pixel you might want to check that the curve is on
the intended side of that pixel.

instruction to adjust the closest point at the
current pixelsize.
